9-85
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-0d35a187.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg">
Vanillin</p>
<p>Balsam of tolu contains 12 % to 15 % of free cinnamic acid, about 8 % of free benzoic acid, 7.5 % of oily liquid (cinnamein) containing benzyl benzoate and benzyl cinnamate. The resinous matter, which constitutes about 80 % of the drug contains, chiefly ester of toluresinotannol. Small quantities of vanillin and styrol are also reported in the drug. The volatile oil obtained by distillation from balsam does not exceed 3 %. The tolu oil is yellow liquid with highly fragrant flavour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="identification">Identification :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>When heated and pressed inbetween two glass slides and examined under microscope, it exhibits crystals of cinnamic acid.</li>
<li>To alcoholic solution of balsam of tolu, add solution of ferric chloride; green colour is produced.</li>
<li>Warm gently about 1 g of the drug with 5 ml of potassium permanganate solution; odour of benzaldehyde is produced.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Balsam of tolu is used as an expectorant and as flavouring agent. It is also an antiseptic. It is a common ingredient of cough mixture. It is used in the preparation of confectionary, chewing gums and perfumery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adulterants">Adulterants :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adulterants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Many a times, exhausted balsam of tolu is added to the drug. Fictitious tolu balsam prepared by adding benzoin and cinnamic acids to the exhausted balsam can be detected by lack of its natural flavour and volatile oil content. Colophony is also added to balsam of tolu. Its presence can be detected by the test for abietic acid, the active constituent of colophony.</p>
<p>Peru balsam is obtained from stems of Myroxylon pereirae (Leguminosae) grown in Central America, Peru and Guatemala. It contains 60 % mixture of balsamic esters (Cinnamein), 35 % esters of balsamic acids with peruresinotannol and vanillin. It is used as an antiseptic, expectorant and in treatment of scabies.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-86
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="h-antirheumatics">(H) ANTIRHEUMATICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#h-antirheumatics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The drugs used to relieve or used in the treatment of rheumatism are known as antirheumatics. Rheumatism (Greek : Rheuma : flowing and ismos - condition) is characterised by soreness, stiffness of muscles, and pain in joints and associated structures, including arthritis.</p>
<p>The modern analgesics and anti-inflammatory agents (like analgin, oxyphenbutazone etc.) used to treat the rheumatism are from synthetic sources. However, the salicylic acid derivatives or salicylates commonly used for the purpose were originally obtained from the plant source i.e. white willow (Salix alba Vulgaris) in the form of salicin, a bitter glycoside.</p>
<p>The herbal antirheumatics which are effectively used in rheumatism, now-a-days, are as follows :</p>
<ul>
<li>Guggul (Commiphora mukul)</li>
<li>Salai (Boswelia seratta)</li>
<li>Nirgundo (Vitex-nirgundo)</li>
<li>Jatamansi (Nardostachys jatamansi)</li>
<li>Colchicum (Colchicum luteum)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indian-bdellium">INDIAN BDELLIUM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indian-bdellium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Synonyms : Guggul, Scented bdellium, Gum guggul</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-source">Biological Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Guggul is the oleo-gum-resin obtained by the incision of the bark of the plant Commiphora weightii (Arn) Bhand, (Commiphora mukul Engl; Balsamodendron, mukul Hook), (Family : Burseraceae).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="geographical-distribution">Geographical Distribution :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-distribution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The plant guggul (shrub) is found well distributed in India, Pakistan Baluchistan and Arabia.</p>
<p>The guggul plant is an inhabitant of dry areas of Rajasthan, Karnataka, Gujarat and Maharashtra. It grows to the height of 2 - 3 metres, much branched with characteristic silvery and paper like bark-peelings. Each plant produces about 0.5 to 1 kg of oleo-gum resin which is collected from January to March every year.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organoleptic-characters">Organoleptic Characters :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organoleptic-characters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Colour : Brown to pale yellow or dull green.</li>
<li>Odour : Agreeable, aromatic and balsamic.</li>
<li>Taste : Characteristic bitter.</li>
<li>Size : 0.5 to 1.00 to 2.5 cm in diameter.</li>
</ul>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-88
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-817d7ecb.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg">
Guggulosterol-I</p>
<p>Resin also contains sterols known as guggulosterol I, II and III.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="standards">Standards :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#standards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Water soluble extractive : Not more than 48 %.
Alcohol soluble extractive: Not more than 40 %.
Ash value : Not more than 5.5 %.
Acid - insoluble ash : Not more than 3.5 %.
Loss on drying : Not more than 11.8 %.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-test">Chemical Test :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To the ethyl acetate extract of guggul add acetic anhydride, boil, cool and add 2 ml. of sulphuric acid, green colour develops at junction due to steroids.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is used as anti-inflammatory anti-rheumatic, hypolipidemic and hypo cholesteremic drug.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="substitutes">Substitutes :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substitutes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Commiphora berryi, Commiphora caudata and Commiphora roxburghii also yield oleo-gum resin of commercial importance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indian-colchicum">INDIAN COLCHICUM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indian-colchicum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Synonyms : Colchicum seeds</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-source-fig-9-51">Biological Source (Fig. 9.51) :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source-fig-9-51" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Colchicum consists of dried seeds of the plant Colchicum luteum, Baker, (Family : Liliaceae).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="geographical-distribution">Geographical Distribution :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-distribution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is found in Western Himalaya, Kashmir and Chamba.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cultivation-and-collection">Cultivation and Collection :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cultivation-and-collection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is found at an altitude of 1000 to 3000 m growing extensively in open lands from Murre hills to Kashmir.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-69
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<p>The plants are cultivated by sowing the seeds in boxes from May onwards. The seeds take a long time for germination. Seedlings are transferred in the field and placed one metre apart. After removing scales and coats, the corms which are also used in medicine, are sliced transversely and dried below 65°C. The collection of the seeds is done from capsular fruits. Colchicum plants flower in the month of August to October and start bearing the capsular fruits from May to July. Capsules are collected before their dehiscence from June to July. During ripening, the seeds become dark in colour and are separated by shifting from the fruits. Seeds are processed and graded accordingly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organoleptic-characters">Organoleptic Characters :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organoleptic-characters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Colour : Dark reddish-brown pitted and sturdy.</li>
<li>Odour : None.</li>
<li>Taste : Bitter and acrid.</li>
<li>Size : 2 to 3 mm in diameter.</li>
<li>Shape : Seeds are globular with strophiole at one side and raphe on the other (Fig. 9.51).</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-4dd36d87.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg">
Fig. 9.51 : Colchicum Seeds</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Colchicum seeds contain about 0.2 to 1 % of total alkaloids, calculated as colchicine. The alkaloids present in the drug are colchicine and demecolcine. The alkaloids have tropolone or cycloheptatrien-ol-one ring structure. Colchicoresin, starch and about 5 % of fixed oil are other contents of the drug.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-7373090c.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg">
R = NHCOCH₃ - Colchicine
R = NHCH - Demecolcine</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-90
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-test">Chemical Test:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>With 70 % sulphuric acid, a yellow colour due to colchicine is produced.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Colchicum seeds are used in gout and rheumatism. Colchicum seeds can control the malignant tumour, but are highly toxic. Colchicine is used to cause polyploidy. It is used in horticulture and in the cultivation of medicinal plants.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="note">Note:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#note" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>B.P. variety consists of dried seeds and corms of plant <em>Colchicum autumnale</em> Linn., a perennial herb and found growing in moist meadows (hence known as Meadow-saffron) in England and Europe. Commercial supplies to seed and corm come from Yugoslavia, Czechoslovakia, Poland and Holland.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="colchicum-corm">COLCHICUM CORM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#colchicum-corm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Synonyms</strong>: Autumn Crocus corm, Meadow Saffron corm</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-source">Biological Source:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Colchicum corms are the corms of Meadow Saffron. i.e. <em>Colchicum autumnale</em> in the fresh or dried form, belonging to family Liliaceae.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="geographical-distribution">Geographical Distribution:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-distribution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is found in England, Central and South Europe.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cultivation-and-collection">Cultivation and Collection:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cultivation-and-collection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In India, <em>Colchicum luteum</em> is used as a substitute for <em>Colchicum autumnale</em>. Hence, the Indian Colchicum differs from the B.P. variety. It is found in Western Himalayas. <em>Colchicum autumnale</em> corms are collected early in summer after the leaves have died. They are prepared by removing the scaly coats. Corms are then sliced transversely and dried at a temperature below 65°C. Indian Colchicum corms are collected from the plants which are two years old and are collected in June and July in Kashmir valley and in the hilly area of Kistwar, Uri and Damel.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organoleptic-characters">Organoleptic Characters:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organoleptic-characters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Colour: Yellowish-brown.</li>
<li>Odour: None.</li>
<li>Taste: Bitter and acrid.</li>
<li>Size: Slices are about 2 to 5 mm in thickness.</li>
<li>Shape: Sub-reniform or ovate in outline or plano-convex (Fig. 9.52).</li>
</ul>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-92
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-antileprotics">(I) ANTILEPROTICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-antileprotics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Leprosy is an infectious disease caused by microorganism known as <em>Mycobacterium leprae</em>, affecting the skin and nerves resulting in disfigurement and deformity of the affected parts. The disease is characterized by glossy, corrugated, thickened skin with decreased sensation of touch.</p>
<p>The drugs used in the treatment of leprosy are known as antileprotics.</p>
<p>Leprosy is completely curable disease, but needs the treatment for long duration of time. Several chemotherapeutic agents including antibiotics are being used at present to treat lepers. Important amongst them are dapsone DDS (diamino diphenyl sulphone) sulfoxone sodium, rifampicin and clofozimine.</p>
<p>Brahmi (asiaticoside) and chaulmoogra oil are the drugs from natural (herbal) origin available for treatment of leprosy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chaulmoogra-oil">CHAULMOOGRA OIL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chaulmoogra-oil" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Synonyms</strong>: <em>Hydnocarpus oil, Gynocardia oil</em></p>
<p><strong>Biological Source</strong>:</p>
<p><em>Hydnocarpus oil</em> is fixed oil obtained from ripe seeds of the plants <em>Hydnocarpus anthelmintica</em> Pierre, Taraktogenos kurzil king. <em>Hydnocarpus heterophylla</em> Kurz and other species of the <em>Hydnocarpus</em>, (Family: Flacourtiaceae) prepared by cold expression method.</p>
<p><strong>Geographical Distribution</strong>:</p>
<p><em>Chaulmoogra plant</em> is native of Myanmar, Thailand and Eastern India. It is also found in Bangladesh. In India, it is grown in Assam and Tripura.</p>
<p><strong>Method of Preparation</strong>:</p>
<p><em>Chaulmoogra seeds</em> contain 40-45 % fixed oil. Seeds are decorticated by machine after grading. The kernels are pressed with hydraulic press and oil is filtered.</p>
<p><strong>Organoleptic Characters</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>Colour: Yellow to brownish-yellow coloured liquid.</li>
<li>Odour: Characteristic.</li>
<li>Taste: Somewhat acrid.</li>
<li>Solubility: Slightly soluble in alcohol, soluble in chloroform, ether, benzene and carbon disulphide.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is white solid below 25°C and soft.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>

9·127
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-80d68e8a.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg">
d-lysergic acid</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-6dbe0183.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg">
ergometrine</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-tests">Chemical Tests :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>To defatted ergot powder, add 50 % potassium hydroxide solution and heat at 170° for one hour, cool, wash thoroughly with alcohol and to it add first iodine solution and then 20 % sulphuric acid; violet colour is produced.</li>
<li>Extract about 1 g of powdered ergot with 10 ml of solvent ether alongwith 0.5 ml of dilute sulphuric acid. Filter the extract and to the filtrate add approximately 1 ml of cold saturated solution of sodium bicarbonate. The aqueous layer becomes red or violet (due to sclererythrin).</li>
<li>In ultra-violet light, ergot powder shows red fluorescence.</li>
<li>Extract ergot with chloroform and sodium carbonate and to extract add paradimethylaminobenzaldehyde, 35 % sulphuric acid and 0.5 % ferric chloride solution. A blue colour is produced (ergotoxine test).</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ergot is used in labour to assist delivery and to reduce post-partum haemorrhage. Ergotamine is used in the treatment of migraine. Ergometrine is also known as ergonovine in U.S.A. It is oxytocic and produces much faster uterine stimulation than other alkaloids. The activity of ergometrine increases with methyl group. Ergotamine and semi-synthetic dihydroergotamine salts are employed as analgesics in the treatment of migraine. Lysergic acid diethylamide (LSD - 25) prepared from lysergic acid possesses hallucinogenic properties.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="storage">Storage :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#storage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ergot should be dried thoroughly and kept in entire form in cool place. It should be stored in well closed containers. Ergot alkaloids are very sensitive to moisture and hence thorough drying of ergot is necessary. The broken sclerotia are very susceptible to the fungal growth and hence broken pieces should not be stored at low temperature in cool place away from light. If powdered ergot is required to be stored, it should be defatted first and then stored or, otherwise, decomposition of active constituents takes place.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9·128
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="q-vitamins">(Q) VITAMINS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#q-vitamins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are the substances which are considered to be essential for the maintenance of normal metabolic functions, but are not synthesized by human body on its own, and hence to be supplied from outside sources. It must be noted that the vitamins received through the normal, well balanced diet are not treated as drugs for a healthy person. But, certain conditions like inadequate intake, increased tissue requirements, disturbances in adsorption or utilization of vitamins reduce their concentration in the body. This leads to certain deficiency symptoms and in such situation vitamins need to be supplied in chemically pure form or their active concentrates. In such conditions, they are treated as drugs of therapeutic nature. Sometimes, they are also given in prophylactic forms.</p>
<p>The excessive use of many vitamins, especially vitamin D, causes toxic effects.</p>
<p>The vitamins are normally not associated with energy formation. They have an important role in several energy transformation reaction in the body. Sometimes, they resemble hormones in their functions and are required in small quantities. The adults, infants, children, pregnant and lactating mothers require a certain minimum level of vitamins in the food called as Recommended Daily Allowances. Chemically, the vitamins largely differ from each other and are grouped as water soluble and fat-soluble vitamins. The water-soluble vitamins are easily absorbed, highly excreted through urine and not stored in body except vitamin B₁₂. On the other hand, fat-soluble vitamins need bile salts and fats for their absorption, normally not excreted in urine and are generally stored in liver.</p>
<p>Cod liver oil, Halibut liver oil are the sources of vitamin A and D, shark liver oil and carrots, in the form of carotene are richest source of vitamin A, while amla contains vitamin C and yeast contains vitamin B complex.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="shark-liver-oil">SHARK LIVER OIL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shark-liver-oil" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Synonyms: Oleum Selachoids</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-source">Biological Source:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Shark liver oil is the fixed oil obtained from the fresh and carefully preserved livers of various species of the shark, mainly <em>Hypoprion brevirostris</em>. In India, <em>Scoliodon</em>, <em>Carcharias</em> and <em>Sphyrna</em> are abundant among the species, and are generally utilised for the extraction purpose. According to I. P., one gram of oil should not contain less than 6000 International Units of vitamin A activity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="geographical-source">Geographical Source:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In India, the sharks (Fig. 9.72) are processed and oil is obtained on commercial scale in Tamil Nadu, Maharashtra and Kerala. Most of the European countries are also producing shark liver oil on large scale.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9·129
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="method-of-preparation">Method of Preparation :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-of-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>With a little variation, the principle involved in extraction of the oil from the livers is uniform in almost all cases. Government factories in Tamil Nadu and Maharashtra process livers for extracting the oil. The livers are cleaned and minced. The minced mass is taken to a boiling pot, where the temperature of 80°C is maintained. The oil extracted is treated with dehydrating agent to remove traces of water.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-79f00ae1.jpeg" alt="img-34.jpeg">
Fig. 9.72 : Shark Fish (Carcharias Species)</p>
<p>The oil is then taken to a vacuum still for dehydration and chilled to separate stearin. Centrifuges are used to separate the suspended materials in oil. The clear oil is manipulated to adjust the desired strength. The oil being sensitive to light and air, all the while, care is taken to minimize its exposure to sunlight and air. Many a times, the livers are stored at very low temperature, until they are taken for processing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="description">Description :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#description" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Colour : Pale yellow to brownish-yellow.</li>
<li>Odour : Characteristic fishy, but not rancid.</li>
<li>Taste : Bland or fishy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solubility">Solubility :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solubility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Shark liver oil is soluble in solvent ether, chloroform and light petroleum. However, it is insoluble in water and slightly soluble in ethyl alcohol.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="standards">Standards :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#standards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The pharmaceutical grade of shark liver oil should comply with the following standards.</p>
<ul>
<li>Specific gravity : 0.912 to 0.916</li>
<li>Refractive index : 1.459 to 1.477 at 40°</li>
<li>Acid value : Not more than 2</li>
<li>Iodine value : Not less than 90</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Shark liver oil contains vitamin A. The concentration of vitamin A in the oil varies from 15000 to 30000 International Units of vit. A activity per gram. Other constituents of the oil are the glycerides of saturated and unsaturated fatty acids.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-131
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="organoleptic-characters">Organoleptic Characters :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organoleptic-characters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Colour : Green changing to light yellow or brick red when matured.
Odour : None.
Taste : Sore and astringent.
Size : 1.5 to 2.5 cm in diameter.
Shape : The fruits are depressed, globose.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-c970f2ea.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg">
Fig. 9.73 : Amla Twig with Fruits</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="extra-features">Extra Features :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extra-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Fruits are fleshy obscurely -6 lobed with 6-trygonus, seeds. They are very hard and smooth in appearance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Amla fruit is a rich natural source of vitamin C and contains 600 to 750 mg per hundred gram of the fresh pulp. Apart from that, fruits also contain about 0.5 % fat, phyllemblin and 5 % tannin. Amla fruits are also rich in mineral matters like phosphorus, iron and calcium. It contains appreciable amount of pectin. The fresh fruits contain about 75 % moisture. The fruits are dehydrated and stored. It is found that vitamin content of dried fruits is not lost considerably. It may be due to the presence of tannins, which retards oxidation of vitamin C.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chemical-test">Chemical Test :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Test for Vit. C : To the aqueous solution of amla, add lead acetate or gelatin, remove the ppt. by filtration. To the filtrate add solution of 2, 6 dichlorophenol-indophenol colour disappears.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Amla fruits are largely used in Indian medicine. It is used as an acrid, diuretic, refrigerant and laxative. Dried fruits are given in diarrhoea and dysentery. They are also administered in jaundice, dyspepsia and anaemia alongwith iron compound. Fruits are also used in preparation of inks, hair oils and shampoo. It is reported that fixed oil from fruits possesses the property of promoting hair growth. Seeds of the fruits are given in treatment of asthama and bronchitis. The leaves are used as fodder. Alcoholic extract of the fruit is anti-viral. It is a popular drug ingredient of ' Triphala ' and ' Chyavanprash '.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9·132
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="r-enzymes">(R) ENZYMES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#r-enzymes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Enzymes are the protein substances, which serve a role of catalysing the biochemical reactions.</p>
<p>Although, they are an essential constituent of living cell, they can act independently. They are colloidal in nature, heat-labile, and highly specific in action. Enzymes are sensitive to pH and to particular substances which act as activators. They are classified according to the type of reaction they catalyse. Normally they are named by adding the suffix-ase to a specific substrate upon which they act. The enzymes are classified into following categories:</p>
<ol>
<li>Hydrolases for catalysis of hydrolytic reactions.</li>
<li>Transferases for the transfer of chemical group from one molecule to another.</li>
<li>Oxido-reductases catalyse the oxidation-reduction reactions.</li>
<li>Lyases catalyse the addition of groups to double bonds or vice versa.</li>
<li>Isomerases are responsible for intramolecular rearrangements.</li>
<li>Synthetases catalyse the condensation of two molecules coupled with the cleavage of pyrophosphate bond of ATP or similar triphosphate.</li>
</ol>
<p>Many of the enzymes also possess non-protein chemical groups. An enzyme moiety comprises of a protein component ' apoenzyme ' and a prosthetic group representing non-protein component. The latter is also called as cofactor or coenzyme. Certain metals and vitamins also act as coenzymes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diastase">DIASTASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diastase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Synonyms: Amylose, salivary diastase, malt diastase.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-source">Biological Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is one of the amylolytic enzymes present in saliva i.e. salivary diastase or ptyalin and pancreatic diastase or amylopsin, found in the digestive tract of the animals (Also known as animal-diastase).</p>
<p>It is also formed during the germination of barley grains and known as Malt-diastase.</p>
<p>Several amylolytic enzymes or carbohydrates of commercial importance are known, many of them are also used in therapeutics. Zymase, maltase, sucrase, cellulase, invertase, hyaluronidase, lysozyme are amongst the important amylolytic enzymes.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9·134
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="description-fig-9-74">Description (Fig. 9.74):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#description-fig-9-74" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Colour : Whitish powder.
Odour : Characteristic.
Size : Unicellular micro-organism measuring less than 1.5 µ.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-7f26638e.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg">
Fig. 9.74 : Budding Yeast</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="manufacture-of-yeast">Manufacture of Yeast:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#manufacture-of-yeast" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Various substrates are used for the commercial production of yeast as mentioned above. But, common and industrially used are beet and cane-mollasses. A suitable strain like <em>S. cerevisiae</em> is grown and it is transferred to sterilised substrate. The equipment is sterilised to get rid of bacteria and other micro-organisms. The nutrient medium on which the yeast is grown is continuously added to the culture medium. It is confirmed that the sugar content of nutrient medium is not more than 1%. The pH is kept in-between 4 to 4.5 and temperature at 25 to 30°C. Nitrogenous nutrients like ammonium sulphate and sugar phosphate are added to the nutrient medium and fermentation is allowed to take place for about 11 hours. Yeast is separated in centrifuge, washed with sterilised cold water, press filtered and finally dried. The moisture content of the final product is maintained at 75% and it is filled in containers and stored at low temperature.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The yeast contains about 65 to 85% of moisture, nitrogenous compounds (proteins), glycogen, fat and vitamins. Vitamins reported are thiamine, riboflavine, nicotinic acid, pantothenic acid, folic acid, biotin etc. The enzymes invertase, diastase, zymase and maltase are present in yeast.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The yeast is used in manufacture of alcohol, beer and various wines and in the bread industry, to raise dough. Irradiated yeast has been used as a source of vitamin D. Glutathion and invertase are also manufactured from yeast. It is a good source of protein.</p>

<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-13a509fe.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg">
Fig. 9.88 : Honey-bee</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="extra-features">Extra Features :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extra-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Yellow bees-wax is non-crystalline solid. It is soft to touch and crumbles under the pressure of fingers to plastic mass. Under molten condition, it can be given any desired shape. It breaks with a granular fracture.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solubility">Solubility :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solubility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is insoluble in water, soluble in hot alcohol, ether, chloroform, carbon tetrachloride, fixed and volatile oils.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="standards">Standards :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#standards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Melting point : 60 to 65° C
Specific gravity : 0.958 to 0.967
Acid value : 5 to 8
Sap. value : 90 to 103
Ester value : 80 to 95</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The chief constituent of beeswax is myricin i.e. myricyl palmitate (about 80 %). Free cerotic acid (about 15 %), small quantities of melissic acid and aromatic substance cerolein are the other constituents. Indian beeswax has the acid value of 17 to 22.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Beeswax is used in preparation of ointments, plasters and polishes. It is used in ointment for hardening purposes in the manufacture of the candles, moulds and in dental and electronic industries. It is also used in the cosmetics for the preparation of lipsticks and face creams. Pharmaceutically, it is an ingredient of paraffin ointment I.P.</p>
<p><strong>White bees wax :</strong> Obtained by bleaching yellow bees wax, should not be used for ophthalmic purposes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adulterants">Adulterants :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adulterants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Very frequently, beeswax is adulterated with colophony, hard paraffin, stearic acid, Japan wax, spermaceti, carnauba wax and several other substances. Adulteration can be detected on the basis of solubility and melting points. The genuine wax should not give turbidity when 0.5 g of wax is boiled with 20 ml of aqueous caustic soda for 10 minutes and cooled.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9·168
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pectin">PECTIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pectin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Pectin is a complex carbohydrate component found in nature in the middle lamella of plant cells, forming colloidal solution in water. Chemically, pectin is a neutral methoxy ester of pectic acid. Pectins are polyuronides and consist of mixtures of pectic substances like proto-pectin, pectin, pectinic acid and calcium pectate. They are obtained from inner portion of rind of citrus fruits or other vegetative matter such as sun-flower, papaya etc. Pectin is a reversible colloid i.e. it may be dissolved in water, precipitated, dried and redissolved without altering its physical properties. Pectin, by addition of water, forms the lumps which on heating goes into solution. The solution is clear to transmitted light and cloudy to reflected light. Under certain conditions, in presence of sugar and acid, it forms jelly like mass.</p>
<p>Pectin is available in number of plants, belonging to different families. Following are few important sources of pectin.</p>
<p>Lemon peel : 10 - 15 %
Orange peel : 10 - 12 %
Apple pomace : 10 - 15 %
Carrots : 10.0 %
Sunflower-heads : 5.0 %</p>
<p>Papaya, guavas and mangoes are also rich sources of pectin. Pectin has several industrial and pharmaceutical applications. Most of the Indian needs are met by import. In India, very few units are manufacturing pectin on commercial scale. U.S.A., Switzerland and other European countries are producing pectin either from citrus peels or from apple pomace. Pectin is standardized on 'gelly-grade' i.e. its 'setting power' by the addition of sugar (100, 150 and 200 gelly grades are supposed to be standard grades for food and medicinal use).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-source">Biological Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pectin is the purified carbohydrate product obtained by acid hydrolysis from inner portion of the rind of citrus peels i.e. Citrus limonis or Citrus aurantium, (Family : Rutaceae).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method-of-manufacture">Method of Manufacture :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-of-manufacture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Depending upon the raw material from which it is to be isolated, process of manufacture needs suitable modification. The type of pectin (i.e. low methoxy group or high methoxy group) needed should also be considered. Following is the general process for isolation of pectin from citrus peels.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-171
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<p>material is then washed with water, put into a cloth bag and extracted with water for few hours by heating on a water-bath at a temperature not exceeding 85°C, as higher temperature and direct heating affect the quality of gelatin. The extraction process is repeated, solution is sedimented and treated with alum, egg-albumin or animal blood to remove impurities like albumin, mucin, mineral matter etc. The purified solution is decolourised with animal charcoal, concentrated in multiple effect evaporator and chilled. Solid mass is cut into strips and dried in vacuum. When the bones are used as the raw materials, they are required to be crushed, extracted with lipid solvent like ether or benzene to remove fatty material and their inorganic phosphates and removed by treating them with dilute hydrochloric acid. The osse in is left in acid solution as residue. This is further limed when collagen gets converted into gelatin. The pH maintained during preparation should be below 7.7. The digested solution is filtered and evaporated under reduced pressure. The gelatin is dried at low temperature.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="description-fig-9-89">Description (Fig. 9.89):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#description-fig-9-89" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Colour: It is colourless or pale yellow.</li>
<li>Odour: Characteristic.</li>
<li>Taste: Slight and broth-like.</li>
<li>Size: It is obtained in the form of shreds, sheets, flakes, and coarse or fine powder. The sheets and flakes are translucent. It is quite stable in air when dried, but is subject to microbial contamination, when moist or in the form of solution.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-691b48d8.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg">
Fig. 9. 99: Gelatin Sheet</p>
<p>It is practically insoluble in cold water, but swells and softens when immersed. It gradually absorbs 5 to 10 times its own weight of water. It is soluble in hot water, in the mixture of glycerin and water and also in acetic acid. It is insoluble in alcohol, chloroform and solvent ether.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9·173
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="geographical-source">Geographical Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Sea-weeds are found in Atlantic and Pacific Oceans, particularly in coastal lines of Japan, U.S.A., Canada, Australia and Scotland. In India, it is found on the coast of Saurashtra. The largest quantity of world production of algin is in U.S. and U. K.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preparation-of-sodium-alginate">Preparation of Sodium Alginate :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-sodium-alginate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The brown coloured algae is used for extraction of alginic acid. The colour is due to carotenoid pigment present in it.</p>
<p><em>M. pyrifera</em>, the principal source for global supply, is a perennial plant that lives from 8 to 12 years, and grows, as much as, 30 cm per day. This giant kelp is found mainly in Pacific ocean. It grows on stands from 15 metre to 1.5 km in width and several km in length. The mechanical harvesting is done, about four times a year.</p>
<p>Alginic acid is present in the cell wall. First of all, the sea-weed is harvested and dried. The dried sea-weed is then milled and extracted with dilute sodium carbonate solution which results in a pasty mass. It is then diluted to separate the insoluble matter. Soft water is only used for extraction purposes, so as to avoid the incompatibilities. It is treated with calcium chloride or sulphuric acid for conversion into either calcium alginate or insoluble alginic acid, which is collected and purified by thorough washing. If calcium is used, it is treated with hydrochloric acid. Alginic acid so collected, is treated with sodium carbonate for neutralisation and conversion into sodium salt. The alginic acid content on dry solid basis varies from 22 to 35 % in all the varieties of brown algae.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="description">Description :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#description" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Colour : White to buff coloured powder.</p>
<p>Odour : Odourless.</p>
<p>Taste : Tasteless.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="solubility">Solubility :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solubility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is readily soluble in water forming viscous colloidal solution and insoluble in alcohol, ether, chloroform and strong acids. 1 % solution of gum at 20°C may have a viscosity in the range of 20 to 400 Centipoises.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="properties">Properties :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#properties" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It loses about 20 % of its weight on drying. Sodium alginate is incompatible with calcium salts, phenyl mercuric acetate and nitrate, crystal violet, alcohol in the concentrations above 5 % and heavy metals. It is also precipitated below pH 3.0.</p>
