<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-c794645a.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg">
Glycyrrhetinic acid (Glycyrrhetic acid)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Glycyrrhiza is used as demulcent and mild expectorant. It is used as a sweetening agent, an antispasmodic, anti-inflammatory and antiulcer drug. It is used as a flavouring agent and for improving taste of bitter medicines like quinine, cascara etc. It is also used in cough-lozenges, cough-pastilles and also as an absorbent pill excipient in the form of powder. Glycyrrhiza does not exhibit laxative property as described many a time, but it potentiates laxative action of senna. One of the constituents of glycyrrhizin, i.e. Glycyrrhetinic acid in the form of disodium salt is used as an anti-inflammatory agent in gastric ulcers. Glycyrrhetinic acid is used in the treatment of Addison's disease. Residual matter produced in the preparation of liquorice extract is reported to have been used as a foam stabilizer in foam type of fire extinguisher. Liquorice is used as a flavouring agent. Ammoniated glycyrrhiza is used as a flavouring agent in beverages, confectionary and pharmaceuticals. Ammoniated Glycyrrhiza is 50 times sweeter than sucrose. However, it cannot be used as a flavouring agent in acidic medium. Liquorice in the form of sticks or rolls is used for manufacture of confectionaries. Liquid extract of liquorice, granulated and spray dried liquid are supposed to be ideal for this purpose.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="picrorrhiza">PICRORRHIZA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#picrorrhiza" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Synonyms: Indian gentian, kutki</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-source">Biological Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Picrorrhiza consists of dried rhizomes of the plant Picrorrhiza kurroa (Scrophulariaceae), cut in small pieces and freed from attached root-lets.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="geographical-source">Geographical Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Picrorrhiza is a perennial herb well distributed in upper Himalayas and also in China. It is found growing naturally in Kashmir and Sikkim. It is also reported in Punjab, Uttar Pradesh and Himachal Pradesh. The drug is collected from naturally growing plants and may be cultivated at higher altitudes (2700 - 4500 m) in Himalayas. It is propagated by seeds and also from rhizomes (Fig. 9.92).</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9·180
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-61e88eae.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<p>The drug is found to contain irridoid bitter substances, picroside I, picroside II and kutkoside. Picrosides and kutkoside are monoterpene glycosides with an epoxy oxide in ring.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Picrorrhiza is used as a valuable bitter tonic, antiperiodic, febrifuge and stomachic. It is laxative in large doses. Alcoholic extract of the root is found to have antibacterial effect. The drug is found useful in treatment of jaundice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="linseed-oil">LINSEED OIL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#linseed-oil" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-source">Biological Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It consists of fixed oil obtained from the dried fully ripe seeds of <em>Linum usitatissimum</em>, Linn., (Family: Linaceae).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="geographical-source">Geographical Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It's origin is uncertain, but it is regarded as indigenous to India. It is cultivated at present extensively as a source of fibres in Egypt, Algeria, Spain, Italy and Greece, while as a source of oil in Turkey, Afghanistan and India. In Russia, it is cultivated for both oil and fibre. (Fig. 9.93).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method-of-preparation">Method of Preparation :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-of-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The variety yielding high percentage of oil is studied for extraction of oil. Seeds are sieved to make free of earthy matter and other matter.</p>
<p>Commercially, linseed oil is produced by use of expellers. Before the seeds are subjected to the expellers, they are rolled into meal, then moistened and heated by means of steam-jacketed troughs filled over the expellers. An average yield of oil is 30 - 35 %. The expressed oil is tanked for a long period to settle colouring matter and mucilage. The oil is then treated with alkali immediately after filtration. Alkali treatment helps to remove free fatty acids. Bleaching of the oil is done by using either charcoal or fueller's earth at elevated temperature. The refined oil produced as above, is chilled to separate wax.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="description-9-94">Description (9.94) :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#description-9-94" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Colour : Yellow coloured clear liquid.
Odour : Characteristic.
Taste : Pleasant.
Linseed oil gradually thickens on exposure to air forming thin transparent film.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9·182
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="caution">Caution :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>To meet requirements of various industries, different grades and types of linseed oil are available in the market. Boiled linseed oil dries at a faster rate and forms smooth and lustrous film. Thus, linseed oil that has been boiled or treated in dryers such as linoleates or resinates of lead manganese, cobalt or zinc should not be used in medicine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adulterants">Adulterants :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adulterants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Linseed oil is adulterated with boiled linseed oil, cotton seed oil, sunflower oil, rosin, mineral fish oils and mustard oil. Fish oil is detected by odour and rosin and mineral oils are detected by studying the composition of unsaponifiable matter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="shankhpushpi">SHANKHPUSHPI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shankhpushpi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Synonyms : Shankhwel, Shankhphuli</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="biological-source">Biological Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This consists of the aerial parts of the plant known as Canscora decussata, (Family : Gentianaceae).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="geographical-source">Geographical Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Shankhpushpi is found throughout India upto an altitude of 1300 m. It is also grown in Sri Lanka and Myanmar.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="organoleptic-characters">Organoleptic Characters :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organoleptic-characters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is much branched annual propagated by seeds. The flowering season of this plant is from October to December. The plant is cultivated in the gardens as ornamental plant for its flowers. This is an erect annual with four winged stems half a metre in length and decussate branches. It grows well in moist situations.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-fcccf207.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg">
Fig. 9.95 : Canscora decussata Herb</p>
<p>Leaves, sessile, 2.5 to 4.0 cm in length, lanceolate decussate, three prominent verticle lines flowers, axillary, solitary white or yellowish.</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-183
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Drug is found to contain bitter substance and an oleo-resin. Two crystalline compounds have been isolated from the aqueous and alcoholic extracts of the plant. Shankhpushpi is found to contain triterpenes, alkaloids and xanthones.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Entire plant, as well as, fresh juice are used in medicine. It is regarded as bitter, alternative and nervine tonic. The fresh juice of the plant is prescribed in insanity, epilepsy, and nervous debility. Alcoholic extract possesses anti-viral activity against Ranikhet disease virus (chicks).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="substitutes">Substitutes :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substitutes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><em>Canscora diffusa</em> distributed throughout India is used as substitute for Shankhpushpi. In gardens, it is grown as an ornamental plant for its rosy flowers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="note">Note :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#note" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some scientists have identified Shankhpushpi as <em>Evolvulus alsinoides</em> (Convolvulaceae). It is a procumbent or sub-erect shrub. Stems are woody at base. Leaves are about one inch long, linear, oblong or mucronate, obtuse, subsessile with tapering base. Flowers are auxiliary, solitary or 2 - 3 together, pedunculate bluish or white coloured, flowering season July or November. Roots are 5 to 15 cm in length, white with penetrating odour.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-e71181ae.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg">
Fig. 9.96 : <em>Evolvulus alsinoides</em> Herb</p>
<p>The drug contains an alkaloid shankhpushpine and volatile oil, in addition to potassium chloride. It is used as brain tonic and sedative.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="garlic-lahsun">GARLIC (LAHSUN)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#garlic-lahsun" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Synonyms : Allium</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="biological-source">Biological Source :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This consists of bulbs of the plant known as <em>Allium sativum</em> Linn., (Family : Liliaceae).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="geographical-distribution">Geographical Distribution :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#geographical-distribution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Lahsun is cultivated in Central Asia, Southern Europe, U.S.A. and India. In India, it is found in almost all the states and cultivated as a spice or a condiment crop.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cultivation-and-collection">Cultivation and Collection :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cultivation-and-collection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Garlic is cultivated in well drained moderately clay loamy soil. It needs cool moist climatic conditions during the growth and dry period during maturity. Garlic is a hardy perennial herb with narrow flat leaves and bears white small flowers and bul-bils. The flat leaves of drug is done by planting bulbs generally, in the month of September to late in</p>
<p>Copyrighted material</p>
<p>A Text Book of Pharmacognosy
9-184
Pharmacological Grouping of Natural Drugs</p>
<p>October. It takes about four months for harvesting. It is also taken as an alternate crop with many other vegetables. For cultivation, about 300 kg of bulbs per hectare are required, and yield per hectare is about 8,000 kg.</p>
<p>India produced 2,86,700 tonnes of garlic in 1987 - 88 alone, in 80,000 hectares.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organoleptic-characters-fig-9-97">Organoleptic Characters (Fig. 9.97):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organoleptic-characters-fig-9-97" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Colour : Bulbs are white to pink in colour.</li>
<li>Odour : Characteristic and aromatic.</li>
<li>Taste : Aromatic and pungent.</li>
<li>Size : 1.5 to 2.5 cm.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251219-e405abb7.jpeg" alt="img-43.jpeg">
Fig. 9.97 : Garlic Bulb</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Garlic bulbs contain 29 % carbohydrates, about 56 % proteins (albumin), 0.1 % fat, mucilage, and 0.06 to 0.1 % volatile oil. It also contains phosphorous, iron and copper. Volatile oil of the drug is the chief active constituent, and contains allyl propyl disulphide, diallyl disulphide, alliin and allicin. Alliin, by action of enzyme allinlyase, is converted into allicin. Garlic oil is yellow in colour and has specific gravity of 1.046. It is optically inactive.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Garlic is used as carminative, aphrodisiac, expectorant, stimulant, and disinfectant in the treatment of pulmonary conditions. It is largely used as condiment. Oil of garlic is used as anthelmintic and rubefacient. Allicin is antibacterial. Garlic oil is useful in high blood pressure and atherosclerosis. It is reported to possess cholesterol suppressing properties.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="extra-features">Extra Features :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extra-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Peduncle is short and longitudinally striated. Involve of three yellowish green bracts and keel are pronounced. Ray-florets (female) are 15 - 23 in number. Disc-florets are 200 - 300 (hermaphrodite), each with 5 lobed yellow coloured tubular corolla.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-constituents">Chemical Constituents :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-constituents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The active constituents of pyrethrum flowers are collectively known as pyrethrins which are organic esters, chemically, made up of carboxylic acid and keto-alcohols. The constituents are known as pyrethrin-I, pyrethrin-II, cinerin-I, cinerin-II, jasmolin-I and jasmolin-II. Pyrethrin-I, cinerin-I and Jasmolin-I, are the esters of chrysanthemic acid, whilst pyrethrin-II, jasmolin-II and cinerin-II are esters of pyrethric acid.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Ester</th><th>Acid</th><th>Alcohol</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Pyrethrin- I</td><td>Chrysanthemic acid</td><td>Pyrethrolone</td></tr><tr><td>Pyrethrin - II</td><td>Pyrethric acid</td><td>Pyrethrolone</td></tr><tr><td>Cinerin -I</td><td>Chrysanthemic acid</td><td>Cinerolone</td></tr><tr><td>Cinerin - II</td><td>Pyrethric acid</td><td>Cinerolone</td></tr><tr><td>Jasmolin - I</td><td>Chrysanthemic acid</td><td>Jasmololone</td></tr><tr><td>Jasmolin - II</td><td>Pyrethric acid</td><td>Jasmololone</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Additionally it also contain pyrethrosin, pyrethrol sesquiterpene lactones.</p>
<p>Commercially available allethrins are the synthetic analogues of naturally occurring insecticides i.e. pyrethrin, cinerin and Jasmoline.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uses">Uses :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a natural contact insecticide. It is used in the form of aerosols containing 0.2 to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">1%</span></span></span></span></span> extract. It is also used in preparation of mosquito coils and sticks and insect repellent formulations. The sprays of 'pyrethrum concentrates' are prepared in kerosene or other non-polar solvent.</p>

<ol start="2">
<li>GLOSSARY</li>
</ol>
<p>Most of the technical terms used for the macroscopic and microscopic descriptions of crude drugs and also to describe their pharmacological and pharmaceutical uses are included in this glossary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-botanical-terms">1. BOTANICAL TERMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-botanical-terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Achene: A simple dry one-seeded, indehiscent fruit with unfused seed coat and fruit wall, but with no special method to liberate the seeds.</li>
<li>Adventitious: Arising from abnormal position.</li>
<li>Adventitious roots: Arising from stems or leaf cutting but not from primary root.</li>
<li>Adventitious buds: A bud which develops in some other place than the axils of leaves or stem apices.</li>
<li>Aerenchyma: Tissue comprising of thin walled cells with large airsacs found in different parts of plants.</li>
<li>Aleurone grains: Protein granules found in plants, quite often in seeds.</li>
<li>Algae: Simple lower plants capable of carrying out the photosynthesis and with unicellular organs or reproduction.</li>
<li>Androecium: Collective term, for the stamens of flower.</li>
<li>Angiosperm: Flowering plant.</li>
<li>Anther: Pollen bearing part of a stamen.</li>
<li>Anticlinal: Situated approximately at right angles to outer surface of plant part.</li>
<li>Annual: Plant that completes its life cycle from seed germination on seed production followed by death, in a single season.</li>
<li>Annual ring: The layer of xylem (wood) formed by one year's growth of cambium.</li>
<li>Annual thickening: Internal thickening of wall of xylem vessel so as to form rings at intervals alongwith its length.</li>
<li>Apical: Of the tip.</li>
<li>Apothecium: Cup-shaped fruit body of certain ascomycete fungi.</li>
<li>Aril (Arillus): Succulent development of stalk or base of seeds of fungi (mycophyta).</li>
<li>Ascomycetes: Group of fungi (mycophyta).</li>
<li>Ascospore: A spore produced by sac (ascomycete).</li>
<li>Ascus: A sac-like structure within which ascospores are produced.</li>
<li>Auxins: Growth regulating substance or plant hormones.</li>
</ul>
<p>(A-6)</p>
